    In One Minute : Hibernate
    Hibernate is the umbrella for a collection of libraries, most notably Hibernate ORM which provides Object/Relational Mapping for java domain objects. Hibernate's primary feature is mapping from Java classes to database tables, and mapping from Java data types to SQL data types. Hibernate also provides data query and retrieval facilities. It generates SQL calls and relieves the developer from the manual handling and object conversion of the result set. The mapping of Java classes to database tables is implemented by the configuration of an XML file or by using Java Annotations. When using an XML file, Hibernate can generate skeleton source code for the persistence classes. This is auxiliary when annotations are used. Hibernate can use the XML file or the Java annotations to maintain the database schema. Resources Official website - Downloads, Tutorials, Documentation, Community, ... Hibernate Wikipedia Article Vlad Mihalcea's Tutorials Hibernate DZone Examples - Step-by-step Hibernate Examples / Tutorials for beginners. Java Persistence with Hibernate High-Performance Java Persistence  ( 6 min )

    Next 13 - Data fetching
    Data fetching is nothing new in Next, but they simplified how this works. You might remember getServerSideProps and getStaticProps from the previous React versions. Those are no longer needed. In return, we get one uniform way of fetching data! The recommended way of fetching data is using server components, as discussed in the previous article. According to the docs, there are a lot of benefits from fetching from server components: Access to backend services like database and API that don't run on the client Keep your secure keys on the server so they don't leak to the client Fetch and render in the same environment Caching your renders on the server Send less JavaScript to bundle One important note is that they recommend you refetch data over passing it down. They changed to use the fetch Web API, which is fantastic. It's a super powerful API, so happy to see this choice. Fetch will always return a promise so we can await the result; by default, it's a cached request/results. Let's show you an example. In our component, we can create a data fetching function that would look like this. async function getData() { const res = await fetch('https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/todos'); return res.json(); } Our component itself can then use this function like this. export default async function AccountPage() { const table = await getData(); return ( ( {todo.title} ))} ); } And yep, that's it, simple. It's also a great abstraction to move towards a unique concern architecture by simply making the components as small and self-sufficient as possible. We also get many options around the fetch API that we can leverage, but it might be best to review them once we need them. Thank you for reading my blog. Feel free to subscribe to my email newsletter and connect on Facebook or Twitter  ( 5 min )

    Make swap better with zram on Linux
    Make swap better with zram on Linux David Both Mon, 11/14/2022 - 03:00 Zram is a compressed RAM disk on Linux. Lately, it's been put to use for swap space on many distributions. In my previous article, I introduced zram and demonstrated how to use it. In this article, I cover some of the ways you can customize how your system puts zram to use. Augmented swap Zram swap can be augmented with standard secondary storage devices. Adding some traditional swap space can be especially useful on systems with low amounts of RAM. (Such augmentation isn't normally useful on hosts with very large amounts of RAM.)     SocialBoat for Women ‚Äî AI Powered fitness game for women
    @SocialBoat Today we launch SocialBoat for Women. Motivation to create this came from my mom's (@seema_jain3) fitness journey. I have seen the hardwork and struggles she put in to get fit and how it essentially transformed her life. Some critical problems that I saw - 1. Lack of time My mom used to manage the home, and this essentially made her mornings and evenings very busy. Mid day is usually too hot to workout outside and fitness centers are usually closed at this time. I would see her get up at 5am :sunny: everyday, to go for her quick 30 minute walk. 2. Lack of relevant programs My mom gained a lot of weight post her pregnancy, and she struggled to find any relevant programs to lose it. Most gyms had male oriented bulk up programs, and fitness classes were usually too intensive for her. She started learning Yoga from a book, and then Pilates from YouTube videos. She tells me it took her 4 years to gain the confidence she had back in college. 3. Her New Program for women After her at home transformation, she learnt jazz and hip hop dance, performed at multiple venues around the country and recently started a fitness program for women called - Yogalates. An amalgamation of yoga, pilates and dance for women. She takes classes on zoom and more than 100 women have joined her program. Scaling up the concept Our goal with SocialBoat is to take some of these learnings and make high quality fitness accessible to >100M women around the country. - A program one can follow from their home - Is accessible anytime during the day - Tailored to women specific needs - Evolves with different life stages Excited to see how people at ProductHunt find it.     Why sysadmins should choose Awesome window manager on Linux Seth Kenlon Wed, 11/09/2022 - 03:00 Awesome is a window manager for the Linux desktop. A "window manager" is a graphical interface that primarily (if not literally) just manages the drawing and arrangement of windows. In practice, even the most rudimentary of window managers actually provides a little more than just the ability to draw a window. Most also provide a pop-up menu so you can launch an application, some provide a dock or panel so you can switch between different applications you have running. They stop short at providing desktop conveniences such as drawing a wallpaper in the background of your screen, mounting and unmounting devices, providing a system tray, and so on.
